#### CW-549256: Huntress Critical Incident | CRITICAL - ISOLATED - Incident on thomas@losbanosrealestate.com (Col...

- Date entered UTC: 2026-03-13 21:28:25
- Closed UTC: 2026-03-15 16:19:10

##### Description

*** The Huntress Platform will revoke all sessions, logging out the compromised identity from the tenant environment in order to prevent attack spread. ***

*** The Huntress Platform will revoke all sessions, logging out the compromised identity, and disable the compromised user from the tenant environment in order to prevent attack spread. ***

If you have an urgent request for support, please go to the link below to place a request a callback from SOC Support.
https://valleytechlogic.huntress.io/org/119401/infection_reports/2013314/soc_callback_requests/new

Organization: Coldwell Banker Kaljian

Incident Report: https://valleytechlogic.huntress.io/org/119401/infection_reports/2013314
Severity: Critical

Investigative Summary:
----------------------
At 2026-03-13 20:26:26 UTC, Huntress detected a suspicious Device Code authentication from the IP address 162[.]220[.]234[.]66 within the tenant environment for user "thomas@losbanosrealestate.com" via the Microsoft Office or Microsoft Graph Application.

User Account
User Account: "thomas@losbanosrealestate.com"

Network
IP Address: 162[.]220[.]234[.]66

Conclusion and Recommendation

Device code phishing exploits the OAuth device authorization flow to grant the attacker persistent access tokens, which remain valid even after a password reset.

We recommend the following actions:

1. Session Revocation: Revoke all active sessions and OAuth refresh tokens for "thomas@losbanosrealestate.com".
2. Credential Reset: Reset the user's password and require re-enrollment of MFA.
3. Application Review: Review and remove any unauthorized applications or service principals granted consent during the compromised session.

Threat Descriptions:
--------------------
Malicious Device Auth Code Usage: An ongoing phishing campaign uses deceptive messaging lures to trick users into entering device authentication codes - which are standard numeric codes typically used to log into an account from an input-constrained device without a web browser - enabling attackers to steal session tokens and gain unauthorized access to corporate data.

Remediations:
-------------
Manual Remediations provided by the Huntress SOC are highly recommended remediation actions to be conducted by your team before resolving the incident in the Huntress Platform:
- Please review the multi-factor authentication devices for this identity, and ensure there are no anomalous devices linked that could form a method of additional persistence for an adversary.
- Rotate the credentials for thomas@losbanosrealestate.com.
- Audit activity for user thomas@losbanosrealestate.com.
- Enable and enforce MFA for thomas@losbanosrealestate.com, if otherwise not enabled.
- Enable complex conditional access policies for thomas@losbanosrealestate.com.

All provided remediations and recommendations can be found in the Huntress Platform: https://valleytechlogic.huntress.io/org/119401/infection_reports/2013314#remediations-tab

Lead Signal Information:
------------------------
Signal Name: Device Code Auth Flow Via The Microsoft Office Or Microsoft Graph Application

Greetings Tom ,

Two summers ago, in July 2023, we officially deprecated the legacy version of**HHC Classic** service and introduced a new transport protocol that is faster and offers improved error correction. At that time, we sent multiple notifications advising customers of this change.

To ease the transition, we kept the old sync server running well beyond its planned retirement. However, that legacy server was finally taken offline two weeks ago. As a result, any remaining users of HHC Classic have now experienced sync failures.

If you are among those affected, please click the button below to learn how to update your software, or click at[**HERE**](mailto:support@handheldcontact.com?subject=Help%20me%20upgrade%20my%20HHC%20Classic) if you have[MobileCare](https://nam02.safelinks.protection.outlook.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Furldefense.proofpoint.com%2Fv2%2Furl%3Fu%3Dhttps-3A__click.crmact.com_s2_001-2D70826422-2D9026-2D4bd5-2Db854-2D521953d768ed_055-2D60d3387a-2D0eff-2D4674-2Dbaba-2D7de7cfddb937-3Fenr-3Dnaahiaduabyaa4yahiac6abpab3qa5yao4ac4adiabqqa3qamqagqadfabwaazaammag6adoab2aayiammahiaboabrqa3yanuac6adfabxaalyaouahaadhabzaayiamqagkadtaa7qa2aaneagoadiabwaa2iam4agqaduaa6qavyapeaeuaduabraamqajiahaadcabdqavqaniafsacyabfaa3aajeagyabqaa6qa7aaoqag6adnabaaa3aan4ahgadcabqqa3qan4ahgadsabsqayianqagkadtab2aayiaoqagkaboabrqa3yanuahyabsab6aazqamiagiabyabsqazqamuadoabnabtaaoiamiageabnaa2aanyamiaggabnabraanaaguadqabnabsaanyagqadiabwaayqaoaameadoabsaayqaniapqadaabvaazaaliameaggabxaa4qamaaheagkabraawqanaameadiabtaawqanaamyagcabqaawqayiaguageabtaawqaoaagyadkadbaa2qamaagyadcadeabqqamyamyahyabqaa2qaoiafuadiabraa3qaniahaadeabvabtaaliageadcabsaazqaliagqadaadbaayaaliameadiabqaa4aaliagiaggadfabrqazaamiadgabwaazqayqamqadmad4aayaamaageac2abxaayaaoaagiadmabuaazaamqafuadsabqaazaanqafuadiadcabsaaniafuageabyaa2qanaafuadkabsaayqaoiaguadgadeaa3qanqahaagkadeab6aamiamiagkabzabraayiagmadqabnabqqanqagyagkabnaa2aaoiameagcabnaa4aamaagmagmabnaa3qayiag4agcabzaa4aayiagiadqabzabsaazaapqaecad4aa-3D-3D-3D-3D-3D-3D%26d%3DDwMGaQ%26c%3DeuGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM%26r%3DZk3IuUALXhOxhs3wTVdwYOn9x-xjVpMC0xJATnWT9s4%26m%3DuOUW9v_RuM1mJjIroTcX6H2BvT0iWlM1GMA9ZKnd0gGYsqCUrALuOjra5SooDdNn%26s%3DmaHZ05p0S4QkBqKwULaF4I3haJ8RR9Gh6xf8ua8ggas%26e%3D&data=05%7C02%7Csupport%40valleytechlogic.com%7Cd79ed64fc6124661016f08de3343e316%7Cf67fcae816d8475f9c711746fb45efed%7C0%7C0%7C639004563884743109%7CUnknown%7CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJFbXB0eU1hcGkiOnRydWUsIlYiOiIwLjAuMDAwMCIsIlAiOiJXaW4zMiIsIkFOIjoiTWFpbCIsIldUIjoyfQ%3D%3D%7C0%7C%7C%7C&sdata=29PGw7XF0G2zE03gLrKbGHUEbHvidmZbaDg6ZziSqJA%3D&reserved=0), I suspect that whatever “budgeting madness” all these managers are going through will be for naught. Their budget submissions will be thrown out when sometime in November or December our wandering CEO commands that his minions cut their departmental expenses, or outright eliminate some offices, to provide funding for his AI habits and his jaunts across the globe. Whatever time they spend driving themselves batty as they try to come up with realistic expense and revenue budgets will have been wasted. It’ll all get tossed out the window and everyone’s budget will be remade to accommodate his demands, which will be untethered from the reality of this association’s financial crisis. Think that’s not so? By January, this place will have lost $10M for three years consecutively, and that’s on top of the losses he piled up while head of ISTE alone.

**From:** Jim Barrett 
**Sent:** Friday, October 10, 2025 11:59 AM
**To:** Genny Ostertag ; Emily Reed ; Mary Beth Nielsen 
**Cc:** Kelly Marshall ; Christopher Logan ; Tisha Ware ; Neil Rowe ; Smita Sharma 
**Subject:** RE: 2026 price increases

Hello,
Has any further consideration been given either to standardizing prices or to increasing them for a select number of titles? If only the standardization goal is to be pursued, because it might involve a smaller number of titles and be less complicated, it must be coordinated with Marketing’s catalog schedule. At this point, it is unlikely that standardization or price increases can be adopted for early January 2026 because the first 2026 catalog is in preparation, and it may be too late to request price changes to be made to it. If either standardization or increases are to be sought for 2026, the earliest that they may be implemented would be spring 2026. That would allow for whatever price changes are decided upon to be reflected in the spring catalog.

Jim

**From:** Jim Barrett
**Sent:** Monday, September 22, 2025 10:41 AM
**To:** Genny Ostertag ; Emily Reed ; Mary Beth Nielsen 
**Cc:** Kelly Marshall ; Christopher Logan ; Tisha Ware ; Neil Rowe ; Smita Sharma 
**Subject:** RE: 2026 price increases

Price increases and price standardization are separate yet complimentary, even overlapping, goals. It makes sense to pursue them simultaneously rather than one without the other. Unquestionably, standardization would seem solely to include price increases for some products. Price decreases for the sake of uniformity or standardization seems out of the question. Thus, by default, standardization is about raising some prices. If that is to be done, it seems reasonable to group those standardization increases with a broader set of products deemed otherwise deserving of an increase.

Given the example of some prices ending in “95 cents and others 99 cents,” achieving no-loss standardization would mean raising the 95 cent-ending prices to match the 99 cent-ending ones. Other price differentials, whether about dollars or cents, could be resolved similarly. The most obvious example involves QRGs and JSGs. The price of Quick Reference Guides was raised in January from 12.95 to 14.95, the first ever QRG price increase. Jump Start Guides are priced at 12.99. Standardization of these identically formatted series would require raising the JSG price to 14.95.

Price increases instituted for reasons other than the pursuit of standardization, would be based upon several factors:

* Increased production expenses, i.e., increases in printing and transportation expenses.

* Broad inflationary pressures on the costs of product development, marketing campaigns, and sales strategies.

* The amount of a product’s previous increase and its percentage of the original price.

* A product’s sales performance, whether sales are declining, moderating, or growing.

* What the market will bear comparisons; in other words, how similar products from competitors are priced.

If these non-standardization price increases are to be applied, they should exclude titles released in 2024 and 2025.

Consideration of price standardization factors and those that may inform decisions about what titles, if any, are to receive cost and market driven price increases should begin as soon as possible.

The larger question of whether the implementation in January 2026 of a program of price increases comparable to those made in January 2025 is to become routine should also be addressed, as should its frequency, whether it be annual, biannual, or something else.

Jim Barrett

**From:** Genny Ostertag 
**Sent:** Thursday, September 18, 2025 6:17 PM
**To:** Emily Reed ; Jim Barrett ; Mary Beth Nielsen 
**Cc:** Kelly Marshall ; Christopher Logan ; Tisha Ware ; Neil Rowe 
**Subject:** RE: 2026 price increases

I agree that given the integration of our two teams we should standardize prices \(e.g., so some don’t end in 95 cents and others 99 cents, so the Guides are consistently priced, etc.\). We also should look at standard bulk discount rates and consider reinstating 25-packs for the QRGs. I’m not in favor of raising prices on everything again like we did for Jan of this year, but happy to discuss this if others feel differently. Adding Neil since he was involved last year in pricing recommendations.

Thanks,
Genny

**From:**Jim Barrett 
**Date:** Wednesday, September 17, 2025 at 10:58 AM
**To:** Genny Ostertag , Mary Beth Nielsen , Emily Reed 
**Cc:** Kelly Marshall , Christopher Logan , Tisha Ware 
**Subject:** 2026 price increases

At the beginning of 2025 ASCD raised prices on a select number of titles. The increases varied, and not by percentage but by dollar amount. They were raised by amounts judged most suitable according to the titles’ current price, age, and sales history.

This project included some discussion of whether scheduled price increases should become routine, as in annual, biannual, or some longer interval, or if instead they should be implemented occasionally, when deemed necessary, and not on a semi-fixed schedule. I am not sure there was a final resolution to this issue.

It is now September and if the idea of again raising prices, effective in January 2026, has come to anyone’s mind, now is the time to begin discussing them and the methodology to be used to determine titles, the amounts, and how to implement the increases, most likely via an IT script.

This discussion might also need to be broadened to include the subject of price increases on ISTE titles.

A schedule of marketing, website, and other public notices advising of the coming increases would also have to be planned. Customer Service and Brightkey would need to be brought in, and specifically about what would be the allowable date range for P.O.s that cite old prices.

It’s a lot to consider and if it is felt that it might be suitable to raise prices again, the discussion of the entire subject needs to begin now.

-Jim
